For those given to worrying about the environment or just wishing to live more simply, the method just described produces no non-recyclable waste. It makes me wonder why more men don't use safety razors, given how cheaply one can get his hands on blades like this. The only less wasteful method is with a straight razor, but the learning curve is simply too steep for my liking.<br /><br />Go to an antique store or go online and without too much trouble you can find gizmos which claim to re-sharpen your razor blade. Perhaps razor blades were proportionally more expensive back in the 20s or 30s; perhaps, however, they never sold really well and were an old-fashioned version of the modern contraptions you see on midnight infomercials nowadays - things that sound like a good idea but when delivered don't live up to the hype. So it is with razor blade sharpeners. I own one and it doesn't extend the blade's life appreciably - certainly not enough to justify the cost.

I shave every day and change blades once per week, which means that this 100 pack will last me almost 2 years! I don't have time for that in the morning. Fortunately, you don't need a brush or fancy cream - good old canned shave cream foam (Barbasol or similar) works fine with DE blades. Heck, use a brush and cream/soap if you're into that sort of thing, but if quick and cheap is more your style, foam is fine.<br /><br />One note about disposal - even a week old DE blade is still VERY sharp! Be careful how you dispose of old blades, as they can easily slice through trash bags and cut someone. I'd recommend keeping a glass or hard plastic container in your drawer and throwing them in there. I use an old glass jelly jar. Then when the jar is full, dispose of jar and old blades all at once.

  723. I have had some time now to compare blades to one another and get a feel for which ones do best in my razor, an Edwin Jagger 89lbl. A pack of 5 Derby blades came with this razor, and it seems that the people at Edwin Jagger know what they are doing. These Derby blades provide a good shave without skin irritation. At a bulk price of less than 10 cents per blade, they are as close to free as you will ever get. There are many shaving snobs out there that act as if shaving is high art. For me switching to shaving with a double edge safety razor and all it involves has made shaving a joy for me and I look forward to it as much as my first cup of coffee in the morning. I have realized a few things so far. Preparation is the most important, just like every other task. A hot shower really does help hydrate the skin. I actually prefer a hot washcloth. It is amazing what you can use a microwave for: a normal washcloth wet, then squeezed out, rolled up and heated for 50 seconds works for me. I also heat a mug of water as my tap water meets the current building code for temperature, which means it isn't hot enough. I heat all this up while making coffee, so no time wasted. Then, and here is the key, I use 4 drops of pre-shave oil, prior to whipping up some shave cream. I currently use Taylor of Old Bond Street Lavender shaving cream, but any good shave cream will work well. After prepping as explained, my shave this morning with a fresh Derby blade is as good as I expect out of any blade. My priorities in a blade are skin protection first, cut whiskers second. I have used Feather blades and they are amazingly sharp, but quite harsh on my sensitive skin. The Derby gives a great shave without the raw feeling of the Feather. I shave only down grain and cross grain. That super smooth against the grain shave isn't worth my face burning the rest of the day. These are excellent blades for me and my beard, and should be an excellent choice for anyone experienced or newto double edge shaving. To anyone is considering purchasing Derby blades, it is a zero risk purchase. At less than 10 cents/blade, even if you change blades daily, they are inexpensive. I get about a week out of a Derby blade and usually change it just because it seems like it's been a while. My last shave with the blade is still a good shave. Enjoy. Save your money for something else, like good beer.

I can only say that for my beard and skin, the Derby gives me a shave as close as anything I've gotten with with other blades, and it does so with very, very little irritation.
